Task instruction sent to agent 
# Task: Analyze Test Coverage Gaps in Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

**Repository:** envoyproxy/envoy
**Output:** Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`

## Objective

Identify test coverage gaps in Envoy's HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) filter chain implementation. The HCM is the core HTTP processing pipeline in Envoy, responsible for routing, filter execution, and response handling.

## Scope

Focus on the HCM implementation in `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` and its test file `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc`. Also consider:
- `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` — filter chain execution
- `source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` — header manipulation

## Content Expectations

Your analysis must:
1. **Identify at least 5 specific untested code paths** in the HCM (with file + approximate line references)
2. **Propose a concrete test case** for each gap (test name, setup, assertions)
3. **Explain why each gap matters** (what bugs could slip through)
4. **Prioritize by risk**: label each gap as HIGH / MEDIUM / LOW

## Output Format

Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md` with this structure:

```markdown
# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

## Summary
[Brief overview of the most critical gaps found]

## Coverage Gaps

### Gap 1: [Title]
- **File**: source/common/http/...
- **Lines**: ~NNN-NNN
- **Risk**: HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW
- **Description**: [What code path is untested]
- **Proposed Test**: [Test name and approach]
- **Why It Matters**: [Potential bugs if untested]

[Repeat for gaps 2-5+]

## File References
[List of key files analyzed]
```

## Anti-Requirements
- Do not fabricate file paths or function names — inspect the actual codebase
- Do not list gaps without proposing concrete test cases
- Do NOT run the tests yourself — write the test file and the evaluation system validates independently

  1003→

   700→// Sends a GOAWAY if too many streams have been reset prematurely on this
   701→// connection.
   702→void ConnectionManagerImpl::maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets() {
   703→  // If the connection has been drained due to premature resets, do not check this again.
   704→  // Without this flag, recursion may occur, as shown in the following stack trace:
   705→  //
   706→  //   maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()
   707→  //   doConnectionClose()
   708→  //   resetAllStreams()
   709→  //   onResetStream()
   710→  //   doDeferredStreamDestroy()
   711→  //   maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()
   712→  //   ...
   713→  //
   714→  // The recursion will continue until all streams are destroyed. If there are many streams
   715→  // that may result in a stack overflow. This flag is used to avoid above recursion.
   716→  if (drained_due_to_premature_resets_) {
   717→    return;
   718→  }
   719→
   720→  if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ == 0) {
   721→    return;
   722→  }
   723→
   724→  const uint64_t limit =
   725→      runtime_.snapshot().getInteger(ConnectionManagerImpl::PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey, 500);
   726→
   727→  if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit) {
   728→    // Even though the total number of streams have not reached `limit`, check if the number of bad
   729→    // streams is high enough that even if every subsequent stream is good, the connection
   730→    // would be closed once the limit is reached, and if so close the connection now.
   731→    if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < limit) {
   732→      return;
   733→    }
   734→  } else {
   735→    if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_) {
   736→      return;
   737→    }
   738→  }
   739→
   740→  i

  1303→  // If recreateStream is called, the HCM rewinds state and may send more encodeData calls.
  1304→  if (end_stream && !filter_manager_.hasLastDownstreamByteReceived()) {
  1305→    filter_manager_.streamInfo().downstreamTiming().onLastDownstreamRxByteReceived(
  1306→        connection_manager_.dispatcher_->timeSource());
  1307→    ENVOY_STREAM_LOG(debug, "request end stream timestamp recorded", *this);
  1308→  }
  1309→}
  1310→
  1311→// Ordering in this function is complicated, but important.
  1312→//
  1313→// We want to do minimal work before selecting route and creating a filter
  1314→// chain to maximize the number of requests which get custom filter behavior,
  1315→// e.g. registering access logging.
  1316→//
  1317→// This must be balanced by doing sanity checking for invalid requests (one
  1318→// can't route select properly without full headers), checking state required to
  1319→// serve error responses (connection close, head requests, etc), and
  1320→// modifications which may themselves affect route selection.

  1326→  // a stream.

117-assistanttext-
The analysis has been written to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`. Here's a summary of what was found:

## Summary of Findings

Six coverage gaps were identified by inspecting the actual source against the test suite. Searches confirmed none of these paths are exercised anywhere in `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc`.

### HIGH Risk

1. **`maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` + `isPrematureRstStream`** (lines ~677–749)  
   The entire DoS-protection mechanism for premature RST stream floods has **zero test coverage** — no test touches `isPrematureRstStream`, the 50% ratio check, the `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` recursion guard, or the `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` stat.

2. **`sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` immediate shutdown path** (lines ~816–823)  
   Only the graceful (`true`) path is tested. The immediate path (synchronous `shutdownNotice` → `goAway` → `doConnectionClose`) and the `go_away_sent_` duplicate-call guard are both untested.

3. **Response header validator `result.new_headers` branch** (lines ~2014–2024)  
   All tests configure `transformResponseHeaders` to return `success()` (null new_headers). The branch that encodes a transformed header map — and the `!result.status.ok()` TODO placeholder — are never reached.

### MEDIUM Risk

4. **`chargeStats()` InternalRedirect skip** (lines ~1078–1083) — No test verifies stats are suppressed for internal redirect streams.

5. **HTTP/1.0 `Connection: keep-alive` injection** (lines ~1940–1948) — The keep-alive path (when `Content-Length` is present) is untested; only the drain-on-close path has coverage.

6. **`validateTrailers()` HTTP/2 `InvalidUnderscore` reset** (lines ~1283–1286) — The H/2-specific code path that resets the stream (instead of sending 400 and closing the connection) is not covered.

If it is the last filter, continue with\n      // processing since we need to handle the case where a terminal filter wants to buffer, but\n      // a previous filter has added body.\n      maybeContinueDecoding(continue_data_entry);\n      return;\n    }\n\n    // Here we handle the case where we have a header only request, but a filter adds a body\n    // to it. We need to not raise end_stream = true to further filters during inline iteration.\n    if (end_stream && buffered_request_data_ && continue_data_entry == decoder_filters_.end()) {\n      continue_data_entry = entry;\n    }\n    // The decoder filter chain is finished here if the following is true:\n    // 1. the last filter has observed the end_stream AND\n    // 2. no filter, including the last filter, has injected body during header iteration.\n    // If body was injected the end_stream will be processed in the `decodeData()` method below.\n    const bool no_body_was_injected = continue_data_entry == decoder_filters_.end();\n    terminal_filter_decoded_end_stream =\n        (std::next(entry) == decoder_filters_.end() && (*entry)->end_stream_) &&\n        no_body_was_injected;\n  }\n\n  maybeContinueDecoding(continue_data_entry);\n\n  if (end_stream) {\n    disarmRequestTimeout();\n  }\n  maybeEndDecode(terminal_filter_decoded_end_stream);\n}\n\nvoid FilterManager::decodeData(ActiveStreamDecoderFilter* filter, Buffer::Instance& data,\n                               bool end_stream,\n                               FilterIterationStartState filter_iteration_start_state) {\n  ScopeTrackerScopeState scope(this, dispatcher_);\n  filter_manager_callbacks_.resetIdleTimer();\n\n  // If a response is complete or a reset has been sent, filters do not care about further body\n  // data. Just drop it.\n  if (stopDecoderFilterChain()) {\n    return;\n  }\n\n  auto trailers_added_entry = decoder_filters_.end();\n  const bool trailers_exists_at_start = filter_manager_callbacks_.requestTrailers().has_value();\n  // Filter iteration may start at the current filter.\n  StreamDecoderFilters::Iterator entry = commonDecodePrefix(filter, filter_iteration_start_state);\n  bool terminal_filter_decoded_end_stream = false;\n  ASSERT(!state_.decoder_filter_chain_complete_ || entry == decoder_filters_.end() ||\n         (*entry)->end_stream_);\n\n  for (; entry != decoder_filters_.end(); entry++) {\n    ENVOY_EXECUTION_SCOPE(trackedStream(), &(*entry)->filter_context_);\n    // If the filter pointed by entry has stopped for all frame types, return now.\n    if (handleDataIfStopAll(**entry, data, state_.decoder_filters_streaming_)) {\n      return;\n    }\n    // If end_stream_ is marked for a filter, the data is not for this filter and filters after.\n    //\n    // In following case, ActiveStreamFilterBase::commonContinue() could be called recursively and\n    // its doData() is called with wrong data.\n    //\n    //  There are 3 decode filters and \"wrapper\" refers to ActiveStreamFilter object.\n    //\n    //  filter0->decodeHeaders(_, true)\n    //    return STOP\n    //  filter0->continueDecoding()\n    //    wrapper0->commonContinue()\n    //      wrapper0->decodeHeaders(_, _, true)\n    //        filter1->decodeHeaders(_, true)\n    //          filter1->addDecodeData()\n    //          return CONTINUE\n    //        filter2->decodeHeaders(_, false)\n    //          return CONTINUE\n    //        wrapper1->commonContinue() // Detects data is added.\n    //          wrapper1->doData()\n    //            wrapper1->decodeData()\n    //              filter2->decodeData(_, true)\n    //                 return CONTINUE\n    //      wrapper0->doData() // This should not be called\n    //        wrapper0->decodeData()\n    //          filter1->decodeData(_, true)  // It will cause assertions.\n    //\n    // One way to solve this problem is to mark end_stream_ for each filter.\n    // If a filter is already marked as end_stream_ when decodeData() is called, bails out the\n    // whole function. If just skip the filter, the codes after the loop will be called with\n    // wrong data. For encodeData, the response_encoder->encode() will be called.\n    if ((*entry)->end_stream_) {\n      return;\n    }\n    ASSERT(!(state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeData));\n\n    // We check the request_trailers_ pointer here in case addDecodedTrailers\n    // is called in decodeData during a previous filter invocation, at which point we communicate to\n    // the current and future filters that the stream has not yet ended.\n    if (end_stream) {\n      state_.filter_call_state_ |= FilterCallState::EndOfStream;\n    }\n\n    recordLatestDataFilter(entry, state_.latest_data_decoding_filter_, decoder_filters_);\n\n    state_.filter_call_state_ |= FilterCallState::DecodeData;\n    (*entry)->end_stream_ = end_stream && !filter_manager_callbacks_.requestTrailers();\n    FilterDataStatus status = (*entry)->handle_->decodeData(data, (*entry)->end_stream_);\n    if ((*entry)->end_stream_) {\n      (*entry)->handle_->decodeComplete();\n    }\n    state_.filter_call_state_ &= ~FilterCallState::DecodeData;\n    if (end_stream) {\n      state_.filter_call_state_ &= ~FilterCallState::EndOfStream;\n    }\n    ENVOY_STREAM_LOG(trace, \"decode data called: filter={} status={}\", *this,\n                     (*entry)->filter_context_.config_name, static_cast<uint64_t>(status));\n    if (state_.decoder_filter_chain_aborted_) {\n      executeLocalReplyIfPrepared();\n      ENVOY_STREAM_LOG(trace, \"decodeData filter iteration aborted due to local reply: filter={}\",\n                       *this, (*entry)->filter_context_.config_name);\n      return;\n    }\n\n    processNewlyAddedMetadata();\n\n    if (!trailers_exists_at_start && filter_manager_callbacks_.requestTrailers() &&\n        trailers_added_entry == decoder_filters_.end()) {\n      end_stream = false;\n      trailers_added_entry = entry;\n    }\n\n    // The decoder filter chain is finished here if the following is true:\n    // 1. the last filter has observed the end_stream AND\n    // 2. no filter, including the last filter, has injected trailers during header iteration.\n    //    NOTE: end_stream is set to false above if a filter injected trailers.\n    // If trailers were injected the end_stream will be processed in the `decodeTrailers()` method\n    // below.\n    terminal_filter_decoded_end_stream = end_stream && std::next(entry) == decoder_filters_.end();\n\n    if (!(*entry)->commonHandleAfterDataCallback(status, data, state_.decoder_filters_streaming_) &&\n        std::next(entry) != decoder_filters_.end()) {\n      // Stop iteration IFF this is not the last filter. If it is the last filter, continue with\n      // processing since we need to handle the case where a terminal filter wants to buffer, but\n      // a previous filter has added trailers.\n      break;\n    }\n  }\n\n  // If trailers were adding during decodeData we need to trigger decodeTrailers in order\n  // to allow filters to process the trailers.\n  if (trailers_added_entry != decoder_filters_.end()) {\n    decodeTrailers(trailers_added_entry->get(), *filter_manager_callbacks_.requestTrailers());\n  }\n\n  if (end_stream) {\n    disarmRequestTimeout();\n  }\n  maybeEndDecode(terminal_filter_decoded_end_stream);\n}\n\nRequestTrailerMap& FilterManager::addDecodedTrailers() {\n  // Trailers can only be added during the last data frame (i.e. end_stream = true).\n  ASSERT(state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::EndOfStream);\n\n  filter_manager_callbacks_.setRequestTrailers(RequestTrailerMapImpl::create());\n  return *filter_manager_callbacks_.requestTrailers();\n}\n\nvoid FilterManager::addDecodedData(ActiveStreamDecoderFilter& filter, Buffer::Instance& data,\n                                   bool streaming) {\n  if (state_.filter_call_state_ == 0 ||\n      (state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeHeaders) ||\n      (state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeData) ||\n      ((state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeTrailers) && !filter.canIterate())) {\n    // Make sure if this triggers watermarks, the correct action is taken.\n    state_.decoder_filters_streaming_ = streaming;\n    // If no call is happening or we are in the decode headers/data callback, buffer the data.\n    // Inline processing happens in the decodeHeaders() callback if necessary.\n    filter.commonHandleBufferData(data);\n  } else if (state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeTrailers) {\n    // In this case we need to inline dispatch the data to further filters. If those filters\n    // choose to buffer/stop iteration that's fine.\n    decodeData(&filter, data, false, FilterIterationStartState::AlwaysStartFromNext);\n  } else {\n    IS_ENVOY_BUG(\"Invalid request data\");\n    sendLocalReply(Http::Code::BadGateway, \"Filter error\", nullptr, absl::nullopt,\n                   StreamInfo::ResponseCodeDetails::get().FilterAddedInvalidRequestData);\n  }\n}\n\nMetadataMapVector& FilterManager::addDecodedMetadata() { return *getRequestMetadataMapVector(); }\n\nvoid FilterManager::decodeTrailers(ActiveStreamDecoderFilter* filter, RequestTrailerMap& trailers) {\n  // If a response is complete or a reset has been sent, filters do not care about further body\n  // data. Just drop it.\n  if (stopDecoderFilterChain()) {\n    return;\n  }\n\n  // Filter iteration may start at the current filter.\n  StreamDecoderFilters::Iterator entry =\n      commonDecodePrefix(filter, FilterIterationStartState::CanStartFromCurrent);\n  bool terminal_filter_reached = false;\n  ASSERT(!state_.decoder_filter_chain_complete_ || entry == decoder_filters_.end());\n\n  for (; entry != decoder_filters_.end(); entry++) {\n    ENVOY_EXECUTION_SCOPE(trackedStream(), &(*entry)->filter_context_);\n    // If the filter pointed by entry has stopped for all frame type, return now.\n    if ((*entry)->stoppedAll()) {\n      return;\n    }\n    ASSERT(!(state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeTrailers));\n    state_.filter_call_state_ |= FilterCallState::DecodeTrailers;\n    FilterTrailersStatus status = (*entry)->handle_->decodeTrailers(trailers);\n    (*entry)->handle_->decodeComplete();\n    (*entry)->end_stream_ = true;\n    state_.filter_call_state_ &= ~FilterCallState::DecodeTrailers;\n    ENVOY_STREAM_LOG(trace, \"decode trailers called: filter={} status={}\", *this,\n                     (*entry)->filter_context_.config_name, static_cast<uint64_t>(status));\n    if (state_.decoder_filter_chain_aborted_) {\n      executeLocalReplyIfPrepared();\n      ENVOY_STREAM_LOG(trace,\n                       \"decodeTrailers filter iteration aborted due to local reply: filter={}\",\n                       *this, (*entry)->filter_context_.config_name);\n      status = FilterTrailersStatus::StopIteration;\n    }\n\n    processNewlyAddedMetadata();\n    // Check if the last filter has processed trailers\n    terminal_filter_reached = std::next(entry) == decoder_filters_.end();\n\n    if (!(*entry)->commonHandleAfterTrailersCallback(status) && !terminal_filter_reached) {\n      return;\n    }\n  }\n  disarmRequestTimeout();\n  maybeEndDecode(terminal_filter_reached);\n}\n\nvoid FilterManager::decodeMetadata(ActiveStreamDecoderFilter* filter, MetadataMap& metadata_map) {\n  ScopeTrackerScopeState scope(&*this, dispatcher_);\n  filter_manager_callbacks_.resetIdleTimer();\n\n  // Filter iteration may start at the current filter.\n  StreamDecoderFilters::Iterator entry =\n      commonDecodePrefix(filter, FilterIterationStartState::CanStartFromCurrent);\n\n  ASSERT(!(state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeMetadata));\n\n  for (; entry != decoder_filters_.end(); entry++) {\n    ENVOY_EXECUTION_SCOPE(trackedStream(), &(*entry)->filter_context_);\n    // If the filter pointed by entry has stopped for all frame type, stores metadata and returns.\n    // If the filter pointed by entry hasn't returned from decodeHeaders, stores newly added\n    // metadata in case decodeHeaders returns StopAllIteration. A recursion guard flag\n  (`drained_due_to_premature_resets_`) prevents the drain from triggering\n  infinite recursion through the `onResetStream \u2192 doDeferredStreamDestroy \u2192\n  maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` call chain. No test in any of the three test\n  files exercises these functions; searches for `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`,\n  `isPrematureRstStream`, `premature_reset`, `PrematureReset`,\n  `drained_due_to_premature_resets_`, and\n  `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` all return no matches.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `PrematureRstStreamTriggersDrainAndConnectionClose`\n\n  *Setup*: Use an HTTP/2 mock codec. Create N streams where each stream resets\n  immediately without ever receiving a response (simulating premature RST\n  floods). Drive `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` past the runtime\n  key `overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count` (default 500) while keeping\n  the ratio of premature resets above 50 %. A simpler variant uses the\n  early-close heuristic: fire enough resets that `number_premature_stream_resets_\n  * 2 >= limit` before reaching the total-count limit.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.value()` equals 1.\n  - `connection_.close(Network::ConnectionCloseType::Abort, \"too_many_premature_resets\")`\n    was called exactly once.\n  - A second call to `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` after the drain does\n    nothing (recursion guard: no additional `close` calls).\n\n  *Second sub-test* `IsPrematureRstStreamWithResponseCodeIsNotPremature`: Create\n  a stream, complete it with a 200 response, then destroy it. Verify that\n  `number_premature_stream_resets_` does **not** increment.\n\n- **Why It Matters**: Without test coverage the following bugs can go undetected:\n  - Off-by-one or wrong operator in the 50 % ratio check at lines 731 and 735\n    allows an attacker to sustain a RST flood without triggering the drain.\n  - A bug in `isPrematureRstStream` could mis-classify every completed stream as\n    premature (or never premature), completely defeating the protection.\n  - The recursion guard `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` prevents a stack\n    overflow; if it were accidentally inverted or removed, production deployments\n    could crash under heavy reset traffic.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Non-Graceful `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` Path\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~797\u2013824\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: `sendGoAwayAndClose` (lines 797\u2013824) has two distinct\n  branches: graceful (`graceful=true`, lines 808\u2013815) and immediate\n  (`graceful=false`, lines 816\u2013823). The graceful path (which calls\n  `startDrainSequence()` and defers the actual close to `onDrainTimeout`) is\n  exercised by the existing test `SendGoAwayAndCloseGraceful`. The immediate\n  path \u2014 which calls `codec_->shutdownNotice()`, `codec_->goAway()`, then\n  `doConnectionClose(FlushWriteAndDelay, absl::nullopt, \"forced_goaway\")`\n  synchronously \u2014 has no corresponding test. Also untested: the `go_away_sent_`\n  guard that suppresses duplicate calls (lines 800\u2013802), which applies equally\n  to both paths.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `SendGoAwayAndCloseImmediate`\n\n  *Setup*: HTTP/2 mock codec. Install a decoder filter that calls\n  `callbacks_->sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` from within `decodeHeaders`.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `codec_->shutdownNotice()` called exactly once.\n  - `codec_->goAway()` called exactly once.\n  - `connection_.close(Network::ConnectionCloseType::FlushWriteAndDelay,\n    \"forced_goaway\")` called exactly once.\n  - Calling `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` a second time (simulating a re-entrant\n    or duplicate call) triggers **no** additional close calls (`go_away_sent_`\n    guard works).\n  - No drain timer is created (unlike the graceful path, which creates one).\n\n- **Why It Matters**: The immediate close path is the \"emergency\" shutdown\n  used when the proxy detects a protocol violation or critical upstream failure\n  mid-stream. A bug here (e.g., missing `goAway()` call or wrong close type)\n  means the client is not properly notified that the connection is being\n  terminated, which can cause the client to retry on a half-closed connection\n  and trigger protocol-level errors. The `go_away_sent_` duplicate-call guard is\n  also entirely untested; if it were wrong, filters could trigger cascading\n  connection close calls.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Response Header Validator Returning Transformed (`new_headers`) Headers\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~2014\u20132024\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: At the bottom of `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders`, if a UHV\n  (Universal Header Validator) is configured, the code calls\n  `header_validator_->transformResponseHeaders(headers)` and then checks the\n  result (lines 2014\u20132024):\n\n  ```cpp\n  if (header_validator_) {\n    auto result = header_validator_->transformResponseHeaders(headers);\n    if (!result.status.ok()) {\n      // TODO(yanavlasov): add handling for this case.\n    } else if (result.new_headers) {\n      response_encoder_->encodeHeaders(*result.new_headers, end_stream);\n      return;\n    }\n  }\n  response_encoder_->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream);\n  ```\n\n  The existing test infrastructure (`expectUhvHeaderCheck`) always configures\n  `transformResponseHeaders` to return `ResponseHeadersTransformationResult::success()`\n  (i.e., `{RejectResult::success(), nullptr}`), so the `result.new_headers`\n  branch is never reached. Dispatch a normal request and have the upstream filter\n  call `encodeHeaders`.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `response_encoder_.encodeHeaders(...)` is called with the **new** header map\n    (containing the added `content-type`), not the original.\n  - `response_encoder_.encodeHeaders(...)` is called exactly once (the early\n    `return` after encoding `new_headers` prevents a double encode).\n\n  *Second sub-test* `ResponseHeaderValidatorTransformationFailureIsIgnored`:\n  Configure `transformResponseHeaders` to return\n  `{RejectResult::reject(\"invalid\"), nullptr}` (failure without new headers).\n  Verify that encoding falls through to the original headers (documenting the\n  current missing-handler behavior).\n\n- **Why It Matters**: The `new_headers` path is the intended mechanism for\n  HTTP/2-to-HTTP/1 upgrade response translation (e.g., converting an extended\n  CONNECT response back to an HTTP/1.1 Upgrade response). Without a test, two\n  classes of bugs are invisible: (1) the early `return` could be accidentally\n  removed, causing the original (potentially invalid) headers to also be sent,\n  corrupting the wire protocol; (2) the TODO failure path has no handling at all\n  \u2014 if a validator marks a response as invalid, the proxy silently forwards it\n  anyway, which violates security and correctness guarantees.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: `chargeStats()` Skips Statistics for Internal Redirects\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1078\u20131103\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: `ActiveStream::chargeStats` (lines 1063\u20131104) is responsible\n  for incrementing downstream response statistics (`downstream_rq_completed_`,\n  `downstream_rq_2xx_`, etc.). Create N streams where each stream resets\n  immediately without ever receiving a response (simulating premature RST\n  floods). Drive `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` past the runtime\n  key `overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count` (default 500) while keeping\n  the ratio of premature resets above 50 %. A simpler variant uses the\n  early-close heuristic: fire enough resets that `number_premature_stream_resets_\n  * 2 >= limit` before reaching the total-count limit.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.value()` equals 1.\n  - `connection_.close(Network::ConnectionCloseType::Abort, \"too_many_premature_resets\")`\n    was called exactly once.\n  - A second call to `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` after the drain does\n    nothing (recursion guard: no additional `close` calls).\n\n  *Second sub-test* `IsPrematureRstStreamWithResponseCodeIsNotPremature`: Create\n  a stream, complete it with a 200 response, then destroy it. Verify that\n  `number_premature_stream_resets_` does **not** increment.\n\n- **Why It Matters**: Without test coverage the following bugs can go undetected:\n  - Off-by-one or wrong operator in the 50 % ratio check at lines 731 and 735\n    allows an attacker to sustain a RST flood without triggering the drain.\n  - A bug in `isPrematureRstStream` could mis-classify every completed stream as\n    premature (or never premature), completely defeating the protection.\n  - The recursion guard `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` prevents a stack\n    overflow; if it were accidentally inverted or removed, production deployments\n    could crash under heavy reset traffic.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Non-Graceful `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` Path\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~797\u2013824\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: `sendGoAwayAndClose` (lines 797\u2013824) has two distinct\n  branches: graceful (`graceful=true`, lines 808\u2013815) and immediate\n  (`graceful=false`, lines 816\u2013823). The graceful path (which calls\n  `startDrainSequence()` and defers the actual close to `onDrainTimeout`) is\n  exercised by the existing test `SendGoAwayAndCloseGraceful`. The immediate\n  path \u2014 which calls `codec_->shutdownNotice()`, `codec_->goAway()`, then\n  `doConnectionClose(FlushWriteAndDelay, absl::nullopt, \"forced_goaway\")`\n  synchronously \u2014 has no corresponding test. Also untested: the `go_away_sent_`\n  guard that suppresses duplicate calls (lines 800\u2013802), which applies equally\n  to both paths.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `SendGoAwayAndCloseImmediate`\n\n  *Setup*: HTTP/2 mock codec. Install a decoder filter that calls\n  `callbacks_->sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` from within `decodeHeaders`.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `codec_->shutdownNotice()` called exactly once.\n  - `codec_->goAway()` called exactly once.\n  - `connection_.close(Network::ConnectionCloseType::FlushWriteAndDelay,\n    \"forced_goaway\")` called exactly once.\n  - Calling `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` a second time (simulating a re-entrant\n    or duplicate call) triggers **no** additional close calls (`go_away_sent_`\n    guard works).\n  - No drain timer is created (unlike the graceful path, which creates one).\n\n- **Why It Matters**: The immediate close path is the \"emergency\" shutdown\n  used when the proxy detects a protocol violation or critical upstream failure\n  mid-stream. A bug here (e.g., missing `goAway()` call or wrong close type)\n  means the client is not properly notified that the connection is being\n  terminated, which can cause the client to retry on a half-closed connection\n  and trigger protocol-level errors. The `go_away_sent_` duplicate-call guard is\n  also entirely untested; if it were wrong, filters could trigger cascading\n  connection close calls.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Response Header Validator Returning Transformed (`new_headers`) Headers\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~2014\u20132024\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: At the bottom of `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders`, if a UHV\n  (Universal Header Validator) is configured, the code calls\n  `header_validator_->transformResponseHeaders(headers)` and then checks the\n  result (lines 2014\u20132024):\n\n  ```cpp\n  if (header_validator_) {\n    auto result = header_validator_->transformResponseHeaders(headers);\n    if (!result.status.ok()) {\n      // TODO(yanavlasov): add handling for this case.\n    } else if (result.new_headers) {\n      response_encoder_->encodeHeaders(*result.new_headers, end_stream);\n      return;\n    }\n  }\n  response_encoder_->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream);\n  ```\n\n  The existing test infrastructure (`expectUhvHeaderCheck`) always configures\n  `transformResponseHeaders` to return `ResponseHeadersTransformationResult::success()`\n  (i.e., `{RejectResult::success(), nullptr}`), so the `result.new_headers`\n  branch is never reached. Similarly, the `!result.status.ok()` failure branch\n  (marked with a TODO) is never reached or tested.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `ResponseHeaderValidatorTransformationProducesNewHeaders`\n\n  *Setup*: Enable UHV via `header_validator_factory_`. Configure\n  `transformResponseHeaders` to return a `ResponseHeadersTransformationResult`\n  where `new_headers` is a non-null `ResponseHeaderMapPtr` containing a modified\n  `:status` header (e.g., replacing `200` with `200` but adding a\n  `content-type` header). Dispatch a normal request and have the upstream filter\n  call `encodeHeaders`.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `response_encoder_.encodeHeaders(...)` is called with the **new** header map\n    (containing the added `content-type`), not the original.\n  - `response_encoder_.encodeHeaders(...)` is called exactly once (the early\n    `return` after encoding `new_headers` prevents a double encode).\n\n  *Second sub-test* `ResponseHeaderValidatorTransformationFailureIsIgnored`:\n  Configure `transformResponseHeaders` to return\n  `{RejectResult::reject(\"invalid\"), nullptr}` (failure without new headers).\n  Verify that encoding falls through to the original headers (documenting the\n  current missing-handler behavior).\n\n- **Why It Matters**: The `new_headers` path is the intended mechanism for\n  HTTP/2-to-HTTP/1 upgrade response translation (e.g., converting an extended\n  CONNECT response back to an HTTP/1.1 Upgrade response). Without a test, two\n  classes of bugs are invisible: (1) the early `return` could be accidentally\n  removed, causing the original (potentially invalid) headers to also be sent,\n  corrupting the wire protocol; (2) the TODO failure path has no handling at all\n  \u2014 if a validator marks a response as invalid, the proxy silently forwards it\n  anyway, which violates security and correctness guarantees.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: `chargeStats()` Skips Statistics for Internal Redirects\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1078\u20131103\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: `ActiveStream::chargeStats` (lines 1063\u20131104) is responsible\n  for incrementing downstream response statistics (`downstream_rq_completed_`,\n  `downstream_rq_2xx_`, etc.). Lines 1078\u20131083 contain an early-return guard:\n\n  ```cpp\n  const absl::optional<std::string>& response_code_details =\n      filter_manager_.streamInfo().responseCodeDetails();\n  if (response_code_details.has_value() &&\n      response_code_details == ResponseCodeDetails::get().InternalRedirect) {\n    return;\n  }\n  ```\n\n  When a request is internally redirected, `encodeHeaders` is still called\n  (with the redirect response), which calls `chargeStats`. The guard prevents\n  double-counting the response since the redirected stream will be charged\n  separately. No test verifies: (a) that `downstream_rq_completed_` is NOT\n  incremented for an internally-redirected stream, or (b) that the final\n  redirected stream IS charged correctly.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `InternalRedirectDoesNotChargeDownstreamStats`\n\n  *Setup*: Use a decoder filter that sets `response_code_details` to\n  `ResponseCodeDetails::get().InternalRedirect` on the stream info, then calls\n  `encodeHeaders` with a 307 response.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_completed_.value()` equals 0 after the\n    redirected encode.\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_3xx_.value()` equals 0 after the redirected\n    encode.\n  - A subsequent normal (non-redirect) encode correctly increments both counters\n    to 1 (validating the full flow).\n\n- **Why It Matters**: If the `InternalRedirect` guard were accidentally removed\n  or its string comparison broken (e.g., by a rename of the constant),\n  `downstream_rq_completed_` would be incremented for every redirect hop,\n  causing overcounting in dashboards and alerting systems. In high-redirect\n  configurations this could cause misleading SLO metrics. Conversely, if the\n  guard were too broad, legitimate responses might not be counted.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: HTTP/1.0 `Connection: keep-alive` Injection in `encodeHeaders`\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1938\u20131948\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders` contains special handling for\n  HTTP/1.0 connections (lines 1938\u20131948):\n\n  ```cpp\n  if (connection_manager_.codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http10) {\n    if (!headers.ContentLength()) {\n      filter_manager_.streamInfo().setShouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion(true);\n    }\n    if (!filter_manager_.streamInfo().shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()) {\n      headers.setConnection(Headers::get().ConnectionValues.KeepAlive);\n    }\n  }\n  ```\n\n  When an HTTP/1.0 response includes a `Content-Length` header (allowing\n  keep-alive framing), Envoy injects `Connection: keep-alive` to signal to the\n  client that the connection will not be closed. While there are tests for\n  `ResponseBeforeRequestComplete10` that check the close behavior when there is\n  no Content-Length, no test verifies the keep-alive injection branch (the path\n  taken when `Content-Length` is present).\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `Http10ResponseWithContentLengthInjectsKeepAlive`\n\n  *Setup*: Configure the mock codec to return `Protocol::Http10`. Dispatch a\n  request. In the filter's response path, call `encodeHeaders` with a\n  response that includes a `content-length: 42` header.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - The `Connection` header in the encoded response equals `\"keep-alive\"`.\n  - `filter_manager_.streamInfo().shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()` is\n    false (connection is kept open).\n  - `connection_.close(...)` is NOT called after the response completes.\n\n  *Companion test* `Http10ResponseWithoutContentLengthClosesConnection`:\n  Verify the inverse: no `Content-Length` \u2192 `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion`\n  set to true \u2192 `connection_.close(...)` called.\n\n- **Why It Matters**: HTTP/1.0 clients rely on `Connection: keep-alive` to\n  decide whether to reuse the TCP connection. If Envoy fails to inject this\n  header, clients may close the connection unnecessarily (degrading performance),\n  or worse, may reuse a connection that Envoy has already marked for closure,\n  leading to request failures. The dual behavior (keep-alive vs. drain-on-close)\n  is entirely untested for the keep-alive path.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 6: `validateTrailers()` HTTP/2 `InvalidUnderscore` Sends Stream Reset, Not 400\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1281\u20131298\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: `ActiveStream::validateTrailers` (lines 1256\u20131299) contains\n  a protocol-version-specific branch at lines 1282\u20131298. When trailer validation\n  fails with `UhvResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidUnderscore`:\n\n  ```cpp\n  if (failure_details == UhvResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidUnderscore &&\n      connection_manager_.codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http2) {\n    filter_manager_.streamInfo().setResponseCodeDetails(failure_details);\n    resetStream();      // <-- HTTP/2 resets stream\n  } else {\n    if (connection_manager_.codec_->protocol() < Protocol::Http2) {\n      sendLocalReply(response_code, \"\", nullptr, grpc_status, failure_details); // HTTP/1 sends 400\n    } else {\n      resetStream();    // Other HTTP/2 errors also reset\n    }\n    if (!response_encoder_->streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()) {\n      connection_manager_.handleCodecError(failure_details);\n    }\n  }\n  ```\n\n  Tests exist for HTTP/1.1 trailer validation rejection\n  (`HeaderValidatorRejectTrailersBeforeResponseHttp1`) and HTTP/2 general\n  rejection (`HeaderValidatorRejectTrailersBeforeResponseHttp2`), but no test\n  covers the specific `InvalidUnderscore` case for HTTP/2 trailers, which takes\n  a slightly different code path (skips the `handleCodecError` call).\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TrailerValidatorRejectUnderscoreHttp2ResetsStreamOnly`\n\n  *Setup*: Use HTTP/2 mock codec. Enable UHV trailer validation. Configure\n  `validateRequestTrailers` to return a failure with\n  `UhvResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidUnderscore`. Dispatch a request with\n  trailers after a partial body.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `resetStream()` is called (not `sendLocalReply` with 400).\n  - `connection_.close(...)` (via `handleCodecError`) is NOT called \u2014 the\n    stream reset is stream-level, not connection-level.\n  - The stream info `responseCodeDetails` equals `InvalidUnderscore`.\n  - Compare with the HTTP/1.1 case: same `InvalidUnderscore` failure triggers\n    a 400 local reply AND a connection close.\n\n- **Why It Matters**: The HTTP/2 `InvalidUnderscore` path intentionally omits\n  `handleCodecError` (which would close the connection), matching historical\n  nghttp2 behavior. A regression that accidentally routes this through\n  `handleCodecError` would cause entire HTTP/2 connections to be torn down on a\n  single bad trailer, causing amplified client impact. Since HTTP/2 multiplexes\n  many requests per connection, this is a correctness and availability concern.\n\n---\n\n## File References\n\n| File | Lines | Role |\n|------|-------|------|\n| `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` | 2,607 | Primary HCM implementation |\n| `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` | 1,989 | Filter chain execution |\n| `source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` | 542 | Header map implementation |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc` | 5,407 | Primary test file |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_2.cc` | ~2,280 | Secondary test file |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_3.cc` | ~2,840 | Third test file |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_base.cc` | 571 | Test base/mixin |\n| `envoy/http/header_validator.h` | \u2014 | UHV interface definitions |\n\n### Key Symbols Cross-Referenced\n\n| Symbol | Location | Tested? |\n|--------|----------|---------|\n| `ConnectionManagerImpl::isPrematureRstStream` | cc:677\u2013698 | No |\n| `ConnectionManagerImpl::maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` | cc:702\u2013749 | No |\n| `ConnectionManagerImpl::sendGoAwayAndClose` (graceful=false) | cc:816\u2013823 | No |\n| `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders` `result.new_headers` branch | cc:2020\u20132023 | No |\n| `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders` `!result.status.ok()` branch | cc:2016\u20132019 | No |\n| `ActiveStream::chargeStats` InternalRedirect guard | cc:1078\u20131083 | No |\n| `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders` HTTP/1.0 keep-alive injection | cc:1940\u20131948 | No (keep-alive branch) |\n| `ActiveStream::validateTrailers` H/2 InvalidUnderscore | cc:1283\u20131286 | No |\n",

# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

## Summary

Analysis of `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (2,607 lines),
`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` (1,989 lines), and
`source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` (542 lines) against the test suite
in `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` (~5,400+ lines across three
test files) reveals six significant coverage gaps.

The most critical are: (1) the premature RST stream DoS-protection mechanism
(`maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` + `isPrematureRstStream`) which has **zero
test coverage**, (2) the non-graceful path of `sendGoAwayAndClose`, and (3) the
branch in `encodeHeaders` where the UHV header-validator returns a *new
transformed* response header map. These three gaps can hide serious correctness
bugs — including connection-state corruption and silent header-manipulation
errors — that cannot be caught by the existing test suite.

---

## Coverage Gaps

### Gap 1: Premature RST Stream Detection and Connection Drain Protection

- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`
- **Lines**: ~677–749
- **Risk**: HIGH
- **Description**: Two related, entirely untested functions protect against a
  slow-RST DoS attack. `isPrematureRstStream` (lines 677–698) decides whether a
  just-completed stream counts as a premature reset by checking whether it
  finished before a configurable lifetime threshold and without sending a
  response status. `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` (lines 700–749) is called
  after every stream destruction and drains the connection (via
  `doConnectionClose(Abort, ...)`) when more than 50 % of total streams have
  been classified as premature. A recursion guard flag
  (`drained_due_to_premature_resets_`) prevents the drain from triggering
  infinite recursion through
... (truncated)
